As she puts it, \"I've always carried around this intense feeling that this was what I was meant to do with my life. I don't know where the feeling came from and I don't remember when it began. I just know that I can't remember a single moment in my life when I didn't feel this way. I never had a choice in what I would pursue; singing pursued me and that was it.\" But she wouldn’t have it any other way. With a vocal style that sounds like a mix of Chrissie Hynde from the Pretenders, PJ Harvey and Norah Jones, she’s gaining well-deserved enthusiastic reviews wherever she plays, from The Meadowlark to Michelangelo’s Wine Bar. Becoming the performer she is now, however, didn’t happen overnight. Now living in Denver, Lindsay decided a few years back to become a Professional Singer. While honing her natural gift, she picked up guitar to allow herself the opportunity to perform publicly. She also began to write her own songs to “try something new” and express herself in way she felt she “wouldn’t necessarily be able to with someone else’s songs”. In early 2009, after spending several months as a solo musician performing around town, Lindsay became a vocalist for The Fever, a successful, local band. Since then, the group gained enough attention that it became necessary to form another band in order to accommodate events. Lindsay now fronts \"3rd Degree\" as their Lead Vocalist, as well as continuing to perform with original group. Her main focus, however, is continuing her successful, solo, acoustic act. This stage in her life and in her music is, “the most fulfilling yet…I can’t wait to see what else happens down the road”. In 2009 Koffi founded 2G Vibe, a multicultural band that performs African fusion music.\nKoffi currently teaches West African drumming and dance classes at CPRD. He is involved in several activities at CPRD, including the International Summer Dance Institute, the Aye youth development program, the annual Granny Dances to a Holiday Drum show, and other performances by the Cleo Parker Robinson Dance Ensemble. book shop'' has several Kerouac events on its poetry calendar. Poets who have performed in this venerable, decades-old series include the late Allen Ginsberg, Bernadette Mayer (who will be in Boulder this summer for the Summer Writing Program), Diane di Prima, Janine Pommy Vega, Anselm Hollo, and many more. The series has always been hosted by poet and Kerouac School alumnus Tom Peters, owner of the Pearl Street landmark ''beat book shop.'' \n\nThe series was hosted for many years by the famous Penny Lane Cafe. In the introduction to Poems from Penny Lane Anne Waldman writes ''One thinks of the legendary Cabaret Voltaire in Zurich where the Dadaist movement was born, or the cafes and bars in San Francisco which spawned the Beat Literary Movement, also the cafe Metro and the Nuyorican Cafe, both in New York City's East Village.''\nThe series currently takes place in the new Laughing Goat Coffeehouse, which has strong ties to the original Penny Lane. Amiri Baraka, Miguel Algarin, Lewis MacAdams, and other poets read there during last year's Summer Writing Program. The Laughing Goat is surely a Boulder literary institution in the making. In the introduction to Poems from Penny Lane Anne Waldman writes ''One thinks of the legendary Cabaret Voltaire in Zurich where the Dadaist movement was born, or the cafes and bars in San Francisco which spawned the Beat Literary Movement, also the cafe Metro and the Nuyorican Cafe, both in New York City's East Village.''\nThe series currently takes place in the new Laughing Goat Coffeehouse, which has strong ties to the original Penny Lane. Amiri Baraka, Miguel Algarin, Lewis MacAdams, and other poets read there during last year's Summer Writing Program. The Laughing Goat is surely a Boulder literary institution in the making. Poets who have performed in this venerable, decades-old series include the late Allen Ginsberg, Bernadette Mayer (who will be in Boulder this summer for the Summer Writing Program), Diane di Prima, Janine Pommy Vega, Anselm Hollo, and many more. The series has always been hosted by poet and Kerouac School alumnus Tom Peters, owner of the Pearl Street landmark ''beat book shop.'' \n\nThe series was hosted for many years by the famous Penny Lane Cafe. In the introduction to Poems from Penny Lane Anne Waldman writes ''One thinks of the legendary Cabaret Voltaire in Zurich where the Dadaist movement was born, or the cafes and bars in San Francisco which spawned the Beat Literary Movement, also the cafe Metro and the Nuyorican Cafe, both in New York City's East Village.''\nThe series currently takes place in the new Laughing Goat Coffeehouse, which has strong ties to the original Penny Lane. Amiri Baraka, Miguel Algarin, Lewis MacAdams, and other poets read there during last year's Summer Writing Program. The Laughing Goat is surely a Boulder literary institution in the making.
